Navy Impounds Customs Vessels 112

…Reasons… (1) Recovering Hydrographic Survey Rights

(2) Customs Detains Navy Materials

The Shanghai Jianghai Customs surveying patrol vessels, "Liuxing," "Jinghai," "Jinghui," and "Jingguang," were impounded by the navy's "Datong" warship at 4 p.m. the day before yesterday and escorted to Gaochangmiao port for berthing. As of 5 p.m. yesterday, they had not been released. A reporter from the Guowenshe news agency went to investigate and met with Navy Vice Minister Chen Shaokuan, obtaining the following detailed record of the impoundment:

"Datong" Goes to Impound. Guowenshe reports that the "Datong" warship, stationed at Gaochangmiao port in Shanghai, received an order from the Naval Ministry on June 19 to impound all Jianghai Customs patrol vessels. The "Datong" immediately set sail with the "Yixian" warship at 1 p.m. on the 30th. The "Yixian" sailed directly to Xiangshan, while the "Datong" sailed to the Huangpu River near Zhaofeng Road. Upon seeing the patrol vessel "Liuxing," it immediately impounded it. At the time, the crew of the "Liuxing," caught off guard and unaware of the reason, could only obey orders. After the "Datong" sent soldiers to escort the "Liuxing" back to Gaochangmiao port, the "Datong" sailed to the river in front of the Ruirong Shipyard and berthed. At that time, the three patrol vessels "Jinghui," "Jinghai," and "Jingguang" saw the "Datong" berthed in a busy area for vessels and, as usual, went to notify it and planned to moor alongside to inquire about the impoundment of the "Liuxing." Unexpectedly, soldiers from the "Datong" boarded the vessels and escorted them to Gaochangmiao together. Therefore, a total of four patrol vessels were impounded and were all berthed in the river in front of the Gaochangmiao Naval Shipyard yesterday. The reporter hailed a ferry to the "Liuxing" and inquired with the crew, who also claimed not to know the reason, only answering that all matters should be inquired at the Customs. The reporter, unable to get to the bottom of it, returned to inquire with the crew of the "Jinghai," who only said that it was about the issue of survey rights. (Also, Huadongshe reports) "Datong" Captain Meng Xiuchun and Deputy Captain Zheng Zhenqian, at 1 p.m. the day before yesterday, led the Jiangnan small vessel from the Jiangnan Shipyard to Yangshupu. At that time, the Customs Marine Department's patrol vessel "Liuxing" was berthed there, about to sail to outside the Wusongkou at 4 p.m. to survey Shentan Shoal. Meng and Zheng immediately sent "Datong" Second Officer Xu Bingjun and He Hui to the "Liuxing" to meet with its captain, ordering it to sail to Gaochangmiao. Because the captain was not there, the other crew members refused to set sail, so the Jiangnan small steamer towed it south, entering the Huangpu River. The Customs River Department's small vessels "Jinghai," "Jingguang," and "Jinghui" also followed on their own. Four or five Westerners from "Jinghai" even boarded the "Datong" to inquire about the reasons. Because Meng and others also did not know the details, after arriving at Gaochangmiao at around 4 p.m., the Westerners went to see First Fleet Commander Chen Jiliang to inquire about everything. Also not knowing the details, they then left. The above, etc., was all talked about by "Datong" Deputy Captain Zheng. Deputy Captain Zheng also said that the "Datong's" internal repairs should be completed within three or four days, and once completed, it must sail to the capital, etc.

Customs Patrol Vessels. Guowenshe reports that the Customs has more than 20 surveying and patrol vessels. The surveying vessels include "Liuxing," "Haixing," "Zhuantiao," "Lijin," and "Pingjin." Except for "Pingjin," which is not often in Shanghai, the other four vessels travel between the Huangpu River in Songhu and sometimes go to Tongchong, Jianghuai, and other places. These vessels are all under the jurisdiction of the Customs Marine Department. The remaining smaller patrol vessels include "Jinghui," "Jingguang," "Jinghai," "Jingheng," and more than 10 others, specializing in patrolling and inspecting merchant vessels in the Huangpu River, under the jurisdiction of the Customs Shipping Office, only in the Huangpu River section, not going outside the mouth. All patrol vessels have existed since the establishment of the Customs and have not changed to this day. The treaty for them was established by Li Hongzhang in the Qing Dynasty.

Chen Shaokuan's Discussion. Subsequently, a Guowenshe reporter learned that Navy Vice Minister and Jiangnan Shipyard Director Chen Shaokuan had arrived in Shanghai in the morning. The reporter met with Chen at the shipyard and asked about the previous events. According to Chen, the navy once had the establishment of a hydrographic survey bureau for hydrographic surveys, without the need for Customs surveys. Now, the Customs is overstepping its bounds and acting as an agent, which is infringing on our sovereignty. Therefore, today's impoundment of its patrol vessels is one reason. Other reasons are that the navy has been building warships for many years, and most of its materials are purchased from overseas. Several times when materials arrived in Shanghai, they were detained by the Customs, demanding taxes. Warships are owned by the state, and the Customs is the Chinese Customs, but they are so unreasonable. Even at that time, the navy paid taxes as required because its materials were not released. At that time, the foreign Customs officials still ignored it and delayed it, which was extremely deceiving. Now, they want to detain our materials and hinder our navy's construction, so we impound their surveying patrol vessels. Moreover, surveying rivers and seas is Chinese sovereignty and should be recovered. This is the second reason. At this point, the reporter asked about future arrangements and whether anyone from the Customs had come to negotiate. Chen replied that no one from the Customs had come. The foreigners from the "Liuxing" disembarked at Gaochangmiao and returned as soon as the vessel was impounded. As for future arrangements, the impounded vessel is a surveying vessel, and our navy already has a surveying bureau, which can be transferred to the bureau for management. In terms of personnel, one more vessel requires employment, which is not a difficult matter. After the discussion, Chen determined that he had to take a merchant vessel to Xiangshan at 5 p.m. for inspection and then said goodbye.

Foreign Staff Negotiations. According to a Huadongshe reporter's discussion with Chen Shixia, a Chinese assistant at the Customs Marine Department, after this incident occurred, Harryman, a British staff member of the Customs Marine Department, not understanding the matter, immediately went with him to the Gaochangmiao First Fleet Command to negotiate. Chen Jiliang received them, saying that he was ordered to handle it and did not know the reasons for the impoundment in detail, but promised to immediately telegraph the Naval Ministry to request instructions on the matter. Harryman and others were satisfied and returned.

Both Departments Express. Regarding the impoundment of the four vessels, a Huadongshe reporter revisited Gullen, a British staff member of the Customs River Department. According to Gullen, the three small vessels of the department that were impounded usually patrolled the Huangpu River surface, and the reasons for the Naval Ministry's impoundment were not known. At the moment, the department has reported the detailed process to the Inspectorate General of Customs for review and handling. Chen Shixia also said that the "Liuxing" patrol vessel is used by the department to patrol overseas lighthouses and transport grain. The reasons for this impoundment were also not known and have been reported to the Inspectorate General of Customs for handling. Gullen and Chen firmly stated at the time that the Marine Department and the River Department were completely unrelated to the Shentan Shoal dredging matter and that this impoundment may be a misunderstanding. The actions of the crew of the impounded vessels were also very free.

Song Ziliang's Discussion. A Huadongshe reporter then visited Song Ziliang, director of the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau, at the National Goods Bank to inquire about the content of the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau's Shentan Shoal dredging and why a dispute occurred with the Naval Ministry. According to Song, he knew nothing about this matter. The Huangpu Conservancy Bureau's Shentan Shoal dredging was for the purpose of developing maritime commerce, approved by the Executive Yuan, and everything was being carried out in conjunction with the Naval Ministry. The Customs' four vessel impoundment had nothing to do with the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau, and the impounded vessels had not received any orders from the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau to survey Shentan Shoal. Therefore, it is rumored that the Naval Ministry's impoundment is related to the Huangpu Conservancy Bureau, but he has heard nothing about it and believes that it may be another matter, not related to the Shentan Shoal matter, etc.

Maritime Affairs Administration Established Yesterday 113

Director Shen Speaks on the Responsibilities of the Maritime Affairs Administration

Encouraging Colleagues to Unite to Seek Development

The Shanghai Maritime Affairs Administration was formally established yesterday, and Director Xi Dingmo officially arrived at the administration to take office. The first administrative meeting was held at 2 p.m. The various situations are recorded below.

Establishment Situation (1) Stand at attention, (2) Sing the Party song, (3) Bow to the Party-State flag and the portrait of Sun Yat-sen, (4) Respectfully read Sun Yat-sen's will, (5) Silent mourning, (6) Director's speech, (7) Staff speech, (8) Ceremony complete.

Director's Speech Briefly stating that the administration was established by order of the Ministry of Communications to manage maritime affairs in the three provinces of Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui. The purpose of the Ministry of Communications in establishing the Maritime Affairs Administration is that our country has historically not paid enough attention to maritime rights, resulting in foreign vessels overstepping their bounds and infringing on our territorial waters. The reason for this is the lack of a specialized management agency. Therefore, at the time of recovering maritime rights, the Ministry of Communications specially established the Maritime Affairs Administration for management, and the importance of its responsibilities can be seen here. However, because of the importance of its responsibilities, it is necessary to implement the spirit and devote all efforts to it in order to achieve results. It is even more important that there are always three types of talented people in society. The first type of talented people do not need to be pushed to act. If they believe that something is their duty, they can do it item by item without waiting for others to direct them. The second type of talented people act only after being pushed. This type of talented people must wait for others to direct them before doing anything and cannot act on their own. The worst type of talented people are those who do not act even when pushed. This type of person not only cannot act on their own but also refuses to act even after being directed. Therefore, it is hoped that all colleagues in the administration will be the first type of talented people who do not need to be pushed to act. There are four points that are expected of all colleagues in terms of service: First, be able to endure hardship. Only those who are persevering, not avoiding difficulties, have the hope of success. Otherwise, retreating will not lead to success. In the future, the administration's work, such as surveying and inspection, must be done without fear of cold and heat. Second, be incorruptible. Public officials should be incorruptible first and foremost, especially in the prosperous area of Shanghai, where dirty things are often heard of. It is hoped that all colleagues in the administration will restrain themselves, advocate thrift, and maintain a pure and unyielding personality. Third, be obedient. No matter what kind of organization, there is always a division of ranks in the system. It is necessary for everyone to be of one mind, with arms and fingers responding to each other, section members obeying section chiefs, and section chiefs obeying the director, so that everything can be done and there is no conflict of duties, and things can be carried out in a unified system. This is another thing that is hoped of all colleagues. Fourth, be studious. The world is changing rapidly, and it is necessary to study at any time to avoid falling behind. All the administration's affairs are specialized knowledge, and this kind of mechanical progress is often a thousand miles away. Therefore, it is hoped that all colleagues will not only gain experience at any time but also study their knowledge to seek progress. The above is only a general outline. It is hoped that all colleagues will invigorate their spirits, unite, and develop our country's shipping industry, etc.

Foreign Vessels Not Sailing to Putuo 115

Customs Refuses to Issue Ship Certificates

Taigu Refunds Tickets Yesterday

Prohibition The British company Taigu specially planned to open the Shanghai-Putuo route this year and has designated the Shanghai-Ningbo line vessel "Xin Beijing" to start the first voyage from tomorrow, scheduled for a total of eight voyages, departing from Shanghai every Friday, arriving in Putuo at noon on Saturday, and sailing back on Sunday. After this matter was announced, the Shanghai-Ningbo Steamboat Tea Room Association telegraphed the Ministry of Communications, requesting a stop to it. The Ministry of Communications forwarded it to the Ministry of Finance, instructing the Jianghai Customs to refuse the foreign vessel's unauthorized entry into the interior. The Jianghai Customs notified the Taigu company that the "Xin Beijing" vessel could only sail to Ningbo as usual. Putuo is not a treaty port and cannot be sailed to. If the vessel sails without authorization, the Customs will stop issuing export ship certificates. The Taigu company, unable to accommodate the facts, completely canceled the proposal to open the Putuo route.

Ticket Refund This time, Taigu's opening of the Putuo route was in response to foreign requests. It was originally planned to limit the number of foreign passengers to 30 each time, with each first-class ticket sold for 50 yuan. In recent days, many Westerners in Shanghai have pre-purchased tickets and reserved seats from the company. Since sailing is not allowed, the company refunded the sold Putuo tickets to the passengers yesterday and explained the reasons for the refund and the situation of not being allowed to sail. The act of foreign vessels entering the interior without authorization has been invisibly dispelled. Many Westerners who want to go to Putuo are now mostly taking "Xin Jiangtian," etc., instead.

Church Property Guaranteed 116

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Has Explanation

Shanghai Catholic Progress Association Chairman Lu Bohong, in view of the fact that after the government announced the Provisional Regulations for the Suppression of Church Property, various provinces, cities, and counties occasionally misunderstood the articles, causing disputes over church property, Lu went to Beijing the day before yesterday to meet with Foreign Minister Wang Zhengting, presented everything in person, and requested an interpretation of the meaning of Article 5 of the regulations. He has now obtained the Ministry of Foreign Affairs' instructions that the church property of various churches, purchased before the announcement of the provisional regulations, is not bound by the provisions of the regulations. The regulations refer to those who purchase land and real estate after the announcement and are subject to the above provisions, etc. The original presentation and instructions are attached below.

Presentation to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs In order to request an interpretation of the articles, protect church property, and maintain good deeds and peaceful religious affairs. It is observed that churches of various countries have established hospitals, schools, orphanages, etc., in the interior, all based on the purpose of philanthropy, widely practicing charity, guiding the people, and greatly benefiting the world and people's hearts. However, the enterprise must rely on expenses to maintain itself. Property is the source of funds. All the churches in various places previously purchased real estate in the interior. Except for hospitals, schools, orphanages, etc., for their own use, the income part is still to maintain the vitality of the businesses they created and to subsidize them for a long time, without any other purpose. Everyone knows it. Freedom of religion is enshrined in the Party constitution and the provisional law. Universal love and equality are the spirit of Sun Yat-sen's revolution. There is no conflict between missionary work and the Three Principles of the People. The church property of various churches should be under the protection of the government. Recently, it has been heard that in various provinces, cities, and counties, ignorant people have caused misunderstandings because they saw that the Ministry's issued Uniform Measures for Foreign Churches in the Interior to Rent Land and Buildings, Article 5, which stated that foreign churches renting land, building or renting houses in the interior, if it is found to have income or business purposes, the governing officials may prohibit it or revoke its lease, etc., which inevitably causes misunderstandings from time to time, taking the opportunity to make things difficult for the church, or even illegally interfering with and disposing of the church property previously purchased. If this continues, it will have a bad impact on both the people and the church. It is observed that the law does not pursue the past, which is the universal rule of the world. The above measures issued by the Ministry were shown to the Minister by the Holy See's representative, Archbishop Gangda, when he paid a visit to the Ministry the year before last. It was clearly stated at the time that only the rental of real estate by the church after the issuance of the articles would be subject to the regulations. The property purchased before the articles were issued would still be allowed to be managed as before, etc. It is requested that the Ministry explain the above articles in detail, so that there will be no more misunderstandings of the articles and encroachment on church property, in order to maintain good deeds and pacify the people and the church. It is appropriate to prepare a document and request the Minister to review and implement it. It is convenient for the public. Respectfully presented to Wang, Minister of Foreign Affairs of the National Government, and Lu Bohong, Chairman of the Shanghai Catholic Progress Association.

Ministry of Foreign Affairs Instructions The presentation has been noted. Article 5 of the Provisional Regulations on the Rental of Land and Buildings by Foreign Churches in the Interior, which states that foreign churches renting land, building or renting houses in the interior, if it is found to have income or business purposes, the governing officials may prohibit it or revoke its lease, etc., refers to the land and buildings rented by the church after the announcement of the provisional regulations. There have been misunderstandings of this article in other provinces, and the Ministry has explained them on several occasions. Let them know. This instruction.

The Market Will Raise Another 250,000 Yuan

Plan to Recommend Fang Jiaobo as the Preparation Director

The domestic goods market's methods are being discussed.

Proceeding Methods The Chinese directors of the Municipal Council, Yu Qiaqing, Yuan Ludeng, the municipal government advisor, Wu Jingxiong, the co-organizer, He Dekui, the chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, Wang Xiaolai, the committee member, Fang Jiaobo, and the market liaison committee members have discussed the results for days, and the methods are said to be (1) raise 30,000 taels to maintain the living expenses of the domestic goods market staff before it opens, (2) the market must strengthen its organization. It has been decided to raise another 250,000 yuan in capital, reorganize, and seek new development to comfort social expectations. Preparations are now underway, and it is planned to recommend Fang Jiaobo as the preparation director, (3) the market has been ordered to close by the Municipal Council, and is awaiting the municipal government's negotiations.

Letter to Chinese Directors The domestic goods market liaison committee sent a letter to the Municipal Council's Chinese directors, Yu Qiaqing and Yuan Ludeng, yesterday, saying, Dear sirs, since our market was illegally sealed by the Municipal Council on June 9, public opinion across the country has been indignant. The Municipal Council is an agency for handling municipal affairs in the concession. Its duty is to protect the safety and security of citizens and to cooperate with the development of industry and commerce. The personnel employed are all supported by the taxpayers. Now, their personnel only know that there are Westerners who pay taxes and disregard the rights of our majority of Chinese taxpayers. Cases of robbery are heard every day, and most of the victims are Chinese. This is the fact of past neglect of duty. Now, it is even worse, and they dare to use illegal methods to infringe on the security of our Chinese taxpayers' businesses and destroy our plans to develop industry and commerce. To infer their intentions, there are other purposes. After reading the newspapers, we heard that the bureau asked the gentlemen to take up the investigation and find a way to mediate. After the gentlemen came to inspect, the bureau adopted the gentlemen's suggestions and asked the chairman of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to invite both parties to report the facts so that the Western directors attending could understand the truth and set a method. Our association believed that they respected the powers of our Chinese directors and the status of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and also hoped that they would reform themselves. We looked at the effects afterward. Unexpectedly, after 19 years, Brown, the representative of the bureau, had an appointment with the Municipal Chamber of Commerce in a letter dated June 22 (Monday), but has not done so to this day. The bureau has already infringed on our national legal rights, and then dared to despise the goodwill of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce. They treat the Chinese directors as toys. Now, after a careful study of the facts before and after the event, it is discovered that the bureau's actions are being manipulated by others. Before and after the event, there are strict organizations. Five copies of the report are attached, as well as the seven conditions submitted to the municipal government. Please check them in detail and urge the bureau to set a method within 48 hours, otherwise, we will only use a consistent and calm attitude to seek self-defense, so as to seek justice and security. There is now a request to the gentlemen that the gentlemen use their position as leaders of the Chinese taxpayers and social organizations to maintain the livelihood of the 600 employees of our market who have been unemployed and the progress of our market's affiliated civilian sales organization, and to strive to provide relief so that the more than 600 enthusiastic patriotic employees can be free from the worry of running out of food, and the poor people who are suffering and have no one to turn to can not lose the opportunity to survive. We have long admired the gentlemen for their concern for helping the poor and relieving the needy, and we hope that they can grant our request. We sincerely speak and await your reply.

Petition of Manufacturers in the Domestic Goods Market 119

The domestic goods market manufacturers association sent representatives yesterday, Hu Shengyao, Liu Zhongying, Tang Rongqin, and Zhou Zhaolin, to the municipal government, the municipal chamber of commerce, the Chinese taxpayers association, and other places to hold letters of petition. The letter said, Dear sirs, the case of the sealing of the domestic goods market has been fortunately affirmed by your righteous words. It is very impressive to see the maintenance of domestic goods. We admire you very much. However, our association has something to say and dares to tell your association. The organization of the domestic goods market is originally divided into two parts: one part is the market's own management, and the other part is the rental by domestic goods factories. At the beginning of the old city hall, almost all were rented by manufacturers. After several reorganizations, the position of manufacturers renting is still more than the position of the market's own management. In May of this year, more than 20 manufacturers rented when moving into the New World, and the fees charged reached more than 2,000 yuan per month, and rent deposits were paid. The business run by the market itself only accounts for one-third of the manufacturers. This time, unfortunately, the Municipal Council ordered the closure due to the equipment problems of the market's attached amusement department. In terms of law and reason, the Municipal Council's handling is indeed inappropriate, but the manufacturers are jointly liable because of their status as tenants, so who will bear the responsibility? Moreover, the manufacturers' participation in the market was originally for the purpose of uniting. Now that misfortune has occurred, for the sake of mutual assistance, the manufacturers have always maintained a whole attitude and dared not make a statement rashly. However, the market has not indicated how far the negotiations have gone and how the manufacturers' losses will be resolved. It is not known that the organization of the market is called for by the United National Goods Factory, and its income is also mainly from manufacturers' rent (this refers to the market, the amusement department should be discussed separately), so-called business losses, since the manufacturers suffered a double one. The outside world does not know, thinking that the manufacturers are insignificant - this is indeed ignorant of its content. Now, we sincerely declare to your association and earnestly request that you uphold justice and provide relief for the manufacturers' losses. For the sake of self-defense, the manufacturers have decided to open a meeting and decide not to rashly operate without a proper method, so as not to shame domestic goods.

The Chinese Merchants' Gauze Exchange Celebrates its Tenth Anniversary Yesterday 120

Yesterday marked the tenth anniversary of the founding of the Chinese Merchants' Gauze Exchange. The exchange was adorned with congratulatory gifts of utensils, calligraphy, and banners from various Shanghai institutions and organizations. A commemorative ceremony was held at 10:00 AM, presided over by Chairman Mu. After ceremonial procedures, Mr. Guo, representative of the Minister of Industry, delivered a speech, as did Mr. Qin, representing the Mayor of Shanghai, and Mr. Xu, the administrator of the Exchange. Guest Mr. Wang Xiaolai spoke on behalf of the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, followed by congratulatory speeches from representatives of the brokers' association and agents. The Chairman then offered thanks, and the meeting adjourned for refreshments. In the afternoon, Kunqu opera was performed at the Great Eastern Restaurant, and in the evening, a banquet was held for the guests, creating a grand occasion. The speeches are appended below.

Minister Kong's Congratulatory Speech: Today marks the tenth anniversary of the Chinese Merchants' Gauze Exchange. I was honored to be invited, but due to pressing official duties, I have delegated Director Guo to attend on my behalf and offer my sentiments in writing to express my congratulations. The Exchange's purpose is to stabilize market prices and regulate supply and demand. In this era of intense commercial warfare, there is a large volume of commodities moving in and out, making a centralized trading market essential to facilitate equitable distribution. Commodity exchanges play this role. In Western countries, the daily market conditions of exchanges are often used as indicators of the national economy's health, demonstrating their immense importance. China's exchange system originated during the First World War.

As prices soared and imports sharply declined, new domestic industries emerged, and commodity exchanges arose in response. The Chinese Merchants' Gauze Exchange is a prime example. Established ten years ago, it has persevered through frequent internal conflicts, commercial decline, and crises in the textile industry, standing tall, leading the market, and contributing significantly to economic and social development with its steadfast spirit. In human terms, ten years old is still infancy, requiring nurturing. Since an exchange's lifespan can far exceed the century of human life, these ten years are just the beginning of its development. Yet, the achievements so far are already remarkable. Future progress, advancing rapidly, should allow it to surpass the exchanges of London and New York. This is my wish. However, I must also add that, as the Western saying goes, "Only steady steps ensure safety." The exchange organization holds the commercial nexus, so its stability is crucial for the national economy's prosperity. Furthermore, China's textile industry is a pillar of modern industry, requiring support amid current market instability. Should the exchange's operations be careless, leading to market crises, China's nascent industry will suffer a setback. I hope those in charge recognize the significance of their mission and approach it with utmost care. They should strive in three areas: first, standardize transactions and regulate trading to curb excessive speculation; second, carefully assess trading conditions to ensure fair and equitable market prices; and third, offer special insights to guide merchants and promote the development of the industry. These points, based on my limited perspective, are presented for consideration. If they are deemed useful and implemented, then twenty, thirty, or even a hundred years from now, we may look back on today's words and assess the future achievements. This would not only be a blessing for Xiangxi, but would also benefit the nation's commercial and industrial enterprises.

Mu Ouchu's Speech: Our Exchange was established on July 1, the tenth year of the Republic of China. Today marks its tenth anniversary. Over these ten years, with the guidance of government officials, the support of clients, the cooperation of brokers, and the collective efforts of our staff, we have reached this commemorative day. Today, on behalf of the Exchange, I sincerely welcome and thank you all for your guidance, support, cooperation, and efforts over the past decade. At the Exchange's inception, I discussed its nature, responsibilities, and functions with you. The Exchange's nature is to act as an agent for buying and selling. The most important point is that neither the Exchange itself nor its employees should engage in any trading beyond acting as agents. Both buyers and sellers must provide margin deposits. Regardless of market fluctuations, the Exchange itself should not incur any risk. The Exchange's responsibility is to safeguard deposits and cautiously extend loans. The Exchange's large capital is solely for guaranteeing the credit of both buyers and sellers and should not be used except for operational expenses. Additionally, margin deposits, additional margin deposits, and special margin deposits generate substantial revenue, making safekeeping crucial. These funds must be deposited in reputable banks and financial institutions and not used for personal favors. The Exchange's function is to stabilize market prices and ensure credit. Anyone can buy or sell by providing margin deposits, preventing market manipulation. Margin calls and special margin calls further secure operations. If someone fails to fulfill a contract, penalties are enforced according to the operating rules. Brokers also provide security deposits. Thus, the Exchange's credit protection is virtually foolproof, unless parties violate regulations. Looking back over the past decade, Shanghai saw a wave of exchange openings, reaching a peak of 147, but only six remain, less than 5%. The rest have been eliminated. In these ten years, our Exchange has strived daily to uphold regulations and preserve credit. Consequently, despite severe market turbulence and intense competition, we have remained independent and celebrate this tenth anniversary. This is something I can proudly report to you. However, as global transportation becomes faster and commercial competition intensifies, our cotton yarn market is not only a benchmark for Shanghai. Due to telecommunications, cotton yarn trading across China is influenced by the Exchange's price fluctuations. The Hankou Cotton Industry Association sends daily telegrams reporting the Exchange's opening and closing prices as a basis for negotiations, a prime example. Therefore, our staff must strive even harder to comply with government laws and the Exchange's regulations as a daily guide. This will directly strengthen the Exchange's credit, ensure operational safety, and indirectly promote the standardized development of cotton yarn trading, eliminating foreign monopoly. Today, on our tenth anniversary, we are honored by your presence. I have outlined the Exchange's past decade and its future aspirations as a self-reminder for our staff and to seek your guidance.

Assassination Case in Shuyuan 121

Victim: Wang Shunong

Around 9:00 PM last night, inside House No. 3, Lane, near the Huolun Mill on Avenue Edward VII in the French Concession, a young man in Western attire was shot and killed in a sudden assassination. The details are as follows: Li Haiyun, a 45-year-old Sichuan native, had been in Shanghai for years, working in Sichuan shops, handling native Sichuan products. Due to misfortune and repeated failures, Li had a novel idea last December, gathering funds with several fellow villagers to establish a small-scale opium den called "Shuyuan" in the kitchen lean-to downstairs at No. 3 Shou Kang Lane, Huolun Mill Street in the French Concession. As a result, many Sichuan natives familiar with Li and addicted to opium flocked to it like ducks.

Qian Product Youth: After Li opened Shuyuan, business was manageable. A few months ago, a Western-dressed young customer arrived, calling himself Wang Shunong, from Guizhou, around 30 years old. He would light a lamp and smoke. Although Wang was addicted to opium, his consumption was minimal, at most about 40 cents worth. With hundreds of customers visiting daily, the den did not inquire into his background. After his first visit, Wang returned to the den every few days or once every few weeks, at no fixed time.

Assassin's Bombardment: Around 7:00 PM yesterday, Wang came alone, took off his Western jacket, hung it on a hook, and lay down on the second bunk, north of the back door facing the street, loading and smoking. Around 8:45 PM, a young man in a white long gown suddenly burst in through the back door, his eyes scanning the room. Seeing Wang lying on the bunk, he suddenly produced a pistol and fired at Wang's face. The ruthless bullet entered Wang's right cheek and pierced his left forehead, leaving a hole.

Detective Investigation: Upon hearing the gunshot, the owner Li Haiyun and his associates and customers scattered and fled. Seeing his objective achieved, the killer seized the opportunity to escape without a trace. Realizing a crime had been committed, the owner immediately reported to the Daximingzhong Police Station. Upon hearing the news, the police chief ordered detectives Wang Licheng and Zhang Ziying to investigate. They found Wang unconscious and immediately sent him to Renji Hospital, but it was too late; he died instantly. Detectives Zhang and Wang questioned Li Haiyun and his associates in detail, all of whom claimed not to know the deceased. No one could clearly identify the killer's appearance.

Business Card Address: Detectives Zhang and Wang removed the deceased's Western jacket and found over ten cards in the left inner pocket, all bearing the name Wang Shunong and the printed address: No. 1456, Sanduo Lane, Changbin Road. There was also a card of Zhang Zhihan and two military train tickets from the Ministry of Military Affairs. Nothing else was found. After the search, the detectives took the den owner Li Haiyun and two associates to the Songshan Road Special Agency. They then went to the Xinzha Police Station to meet with the on-duty detectives and proceeded to Sanduo Lane for a detailed investigation. They found No. 1456, where four women were playing mahjong in the main room. When asked if a Mr. Wang lived there, one woman replied that the house was occupied by a Mr. Jiang alone and that no one named Wang lived there. The detectives explained their purpose, which annoyed the woman. At the same time, sounds of singing arose from upstairs, saying, "How could there be a Mr. Wang here?" followed by foreign language. Shortly, a stout Westerner around 40 years old and a fashionable woman came downstairs.

Wang Moves Out: Upon seeing the detectives, the Westerner asked the reason for their visit and requested to see their cards. At this moment, the fashionable woman suddenly seemed to realize something and exclaimed, "I understand now! A Mr. Wang did live here, but he moved out three years ago. His name was Wang Shunong, and he lived in the attic for only two months. He changed a woman every day to live with him, and we heard him spouting communist rhetoric, so we asked him to leave."

Woman's Testimony: After hearing this, the detectives asked the fashionable woman her name. She said her name was Jiang Meina and pointed to the stout Westerner, saying, "That's my husband," with a joyful expression. The reporter left, sweating profusely. The deceased had moved out of Sanduo Lane three years ago but still used the address, the reason for which outsiders could not know. The body has been transported to the Tongren Fuyuan branch for examination today.

Continued Trial of the Qu Ma Case 122

Two Victims Identify the American Soldier as the Assailant

Qu Relates the Circumstances of His Injury

Yesterday at 10:00 AM, the military court of the U.S. Marine Corps held the second hearing of the Qu Ma case, in which an American soldier was accused of assault, at the barracks on Haifang Road. The hearing adjourned after more than two hours. The witnesses summoned were the victims, Ma Chengbu and Qu Shixiang. Although their wounds had healed, both Ma and Qu had scars about a foot long on their lower left jaws, Ma's wound being particularly deep. Ma and Qu both identified the American soldier as the assailant without error. First, Ma Chengbu related the details of his injury, stating that in the late evening of May 26, he saw an American soldier chasing a shopkeeper, Qu Haigou, at the intersection of Avenue Embankment and Seymour Road. He stepped forward to dissuade him. The American soldier punched him in the nose, causing him to bleed. The American soldier then took a rickshaw eastward. Because he was injured, he stopped the rickshaw, demanding that the American soldier go to the military officer or the police station to argue why he had beaten someone who was trying to mediate. At that time, a patrolling officer arrived and advised Ma to let it go, saying that he was a foreigner and to let it slide. The shopkeeper, Qu Shixiang, also came to advise Ma to return to the store. Ma refused because his nose had been injured and was bleeding, and he insisted on reason. At this time, another foreign soldier and a civilian foreigner got off a tram and pushed him aside, allowing the American soldier who had assaulted him to leave by rickshaw. Shortly after, the two newcomers also tried to leave by rickshaw, but Ma grabbed the rickshaw of the civilian foreigner and refused to let go, questioning why they were helping the American soldier who had assaulted him to escape. The civilian foreigner then took out a knife and stabbed wildly, hitting him four times, twice on the lower left jaw, once in the chest, and once on the left arm, causing heavy bleeding and fainting. Qu Shixiang testified that he initially thought the foreigner was just cursing, but he did not know he had a knife. He stepped forward to dissuade him and was also stabbed twice, once in the lower left jaw and once in the chest. The two assailants then drove east. Finally, Ma Chengbu regained consciousness and was helped by two people to a bar on Gordon Road, where he saw the assailant inside. Ma sat on the escalator and fainted again. The prosecutor asked how many people were present at the time. Ma and Qu answered the same, saying there were only about a dozen pedestrians. The court then adjourned. There are still ten witnesses to be summoned: two patrol officers, Nos. 811 and 2125, rickshaw driver Tan Fulin, tailor Wang Shuyou, tram driver Lu Shanxiang, four Western detectives, and U.S. Army Captain Tiersley. The hearing will continue today and will take several days to complete.

Tian Shulan Sets Off on a Tour of the Country 123

Departed from the North Station at 12:00 Noon Yesterday

Mr. Tian Shulan, a professor at Minzhi Middle School in Shanghai, embarked on a six-year tour of the country. He departed from Shanghai North Station by bicycle at 12:00 noon yesterday. The details of yesterday's events are as follows:

Arrival at the Station: After 10:00 AM yesterday, dozens of Minzhi teachers and students went to the plaza at North Station, holding flags to welcome him. Relatives and friends of Mr. Tian arrived one after another, numbering about thirty or forty. At 11:30 AM, Mr. Tian arrived by car. Photographers took pictures of Mr. Tian, front and back. Shortly after, firecrackers were lit. Mr. Tian then left the station by car, heading to Baoshan Road Station. An escort team of eight students on bicycles accompanied him, returning to Shanghai after Songjiang.

Source of Travel Expenses: As a man of modest means, Mr. Tian's source of funding for his tour of the country is a topic of interest. It is understood that, apart from some travel expenses provided by Minzhi, he adheres to the principle of "no fundraising, no subsidies." He sets off alone, relying solely on the sale of travel route maps and travel photos for his journey. These items will be purchased by schools and institutions in various places. He will also use the proceeds from his travelogue to supplement his expenses.

Collecting Materials: Before his departure, Mr. Tian prepared various forms, such as travel survey forms, city survey forms, and folk art collection forms, to facilitate data collection and compilation during his travels. He will organize and compile his findings, with the goal of informing the nation.

Elementary School Student Escapes Kidnapping 124

Claims to Have Escaped While the Bandits Were Asleep

Family Claims Losses Exceed 50,000

Wang Ruibao, son of Wang Zhengguo, a Ningbo native and former dye merchant residing at No. 1451 Zhonghua Road, Nanshi, was kidnapped on the 12th of last month while on his way to school in his private rickshaw. The incident occurred near the Siming Guildhall on Xinqiao Street in the French Concession. The kidnappers used a car rented from the Zhongshan Motor Company at No. 295 Zhapu Road. They then forced the driver, Wang Youfu, out of the car in a remote area of Xietu Road. The details have been reported in this newspaper. Two weeks have passed since the incident, with no news. Until yesterday morning, the hostage's family reported to the No. 2 Sub-District of the No. 2 District that Wang Ruibao had escaped the previous night around 9:00 PM while the bandits were asleep. According to the young hostage, he was taken to a two-story Shikumen house after being kidnapped. After two days, he was moved to a more secluded location, but he could not identify the names of either place. He said that he was treated well in the bandits' lair. Around 9:00 PM two nights ago, one of the bandits suddenly said to him, "Tonight you can go home. But if anyone asks you how you escaped, just say you escaped while we were asleep." Shortly after, they released him and hired a rickshaw for him. On the way, the hostage asked the rickshaw driver for the name of the area. The driver said it was near the Yiyuan Dog Racing Track. Director Zhang immediately submitted a report to the Director of Police. However, according to those close to the hostage's family, there had been numerous negotiations since Ruibao's kidnapping, resulting in losses exceeding 50,000.

Ms. Wang Guifen, Daughter of Martyr Qiu Jin and Female Aviator, Arrives in Shanghai 125

Soon to Depart for France and Italy for Further Studies

Ms. Wang Guifen, daughter of revolutionary martyr Qiu Jin, is the first Chinese woman to pursue a career in aviation. After studying aeronautics at New York University in the United States for several years, she has returned to China, arriving in Shanghai recently aboard the Changxing Company's Empress of Russia. A reporter from the New Voice Society met her at her residence yesterday, where she discussed her aviation experiences in detail. Ms. Wang stated that she studied aircraft manufacturing and aeronautical knowledge at New York University for over two years. She is skilled in the manufacture of modern single-wing, biplane, naval, military, and transport aircraft. However, she was unable to study the manufacture of the latest American invention, silent camouflage (which releases colored smoke similar to clouds to conceal the aircraft in flight), as the Americans keep these military secrets to themselves. Many American women are engaged in aviation and are very adventurous. The government strongly promotes aviation. The US government has established meteorological stations specifically for aviation across the country, which report weather, wind, rain, and fog daily to ensure aviation safety. Ms. Wang has collected many books on weather measurement, aviation school organization, aircraft manufacturing, aerial radio, and aerial navigation methods, which she plans to translate for those in China who are interested in studying aviation. She plans to leave Shanghai soon for Europe to continue her aeronautical studies at the most famous aviation schools in Italy and France. Upon returning to China, she hopes to work with the government to promote the development of aviation and encourage Chinese women to emulate the courage and adventurousness of American women in pursuing aviation. It is also reported that Ms. Wang is skilled in boxing.

Summer Office Hours for the Two Courts 126

8:00 AM to 12:00 Noon

The Second Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the Special District Court have advanced their office hours, starting yesterday and lasting for two months until August 31. Office hours will be from 8:00 AM to 12:00 Noon daily. In the afternoon, only the traffic, health, and other courts of the Special District Court on Tuesdays, Thursdays, and Fridays, and the appellate collegial court for summary cases on Mondays and Tuesdays, will hold regular hearings. Otherwise, unless there are particularly urgent cases, there will be complete rest. Since public and private criminal suits are concentrated in the morning, the Special District Court's existing criminal court is deeply concerned about being insufficient. It has temporarily borrowed the former No. 3 Court from the High Court for use when needed. The two courts have also established a rotating duty system for judges and prosecutors during the summer vacation to ensure public service.

Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department Offers Free Vaccinations for Workers 130

Factories Please Note

The Shanghai Municipal Council Health Department has formed two teams that rotate through various districts of the Public Concession to provide free cholera vaccinations. In June, they vaccinated a total of 31,000 people, mostly workers. However, many schools also vaccinated students before the holidays. Fewer women were vaccinated, with a ratio of about 1:3 compared to men, indicating that female workers in larger factories are not paying enough attention to prevention. To facilitate vaccinations for workers, the Health Department will send personnel with the necessary supplies to factories upon notification. According to reports, the vaccine's reaction in workers does not disrupt their work or reduce their efficiency.

Brother Sues Brother Over Unclear Inheritance Accounts 131

Seeking to Reconcile Four Types of Accounts

Defendant Hires Lawyer to Defend

Guo Bichen, owner of the Guo Yuanmao Earth Shop and a Cantonese native, passed away in the 11th year of the Republic of China, leaving a substantial inheritance. After reserving a portion for ancestral rites, the remainder was divided among his sons, Qiaoqing, Songqing, Xuanqian, Jianqian, and Fenxi. Xuanqian was entrusted with managing the ancestral property. Now, after ten years without a report, Songqing is dissatisfied and has hired lawyers Jiang Yinian and Wu Guoan to sue Xuanqian, requesting that the ancestral property accounts be submitted for reconciliation. There are four types of accounts: (1) 8,000 taels of shares in the Qianyuandejizhuang and 6,000 taels of shares in the Shenda Flour Mill. These two amounts were divided into four shares, and the plaintiff should receive 3,500 taels. (2) the Sendadong Pawnshop, Qianmaodong Pawnshop, and ChaoYang's Ziadong Pawnshop were all established solely by Bichen. The account books from previous years should be submitted for liquidation. (3) When Guangyu Money Exchange closed, it owed over 100,000. Xuanqian handled the collection of debts. The actual amount collected was never reported and should be reconciled. (4) Guangyu still has over 180,000 in cash. Over 8,000 taels were taken out as public property. This amount should also be divided into four shares, and the plaintiff should receive over 2,000 taels. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenyong of the Special District Court presided over the hearing. After the plaintiff's lawyer stated each count of the lawsuit, the defendant defended each count. He claimed that the Ziadong Pawnshop was jointly owned with his cousin Liu Xihong. The important account books were destroyed by communist bandits years ago, and Liu concealed the proceeds, so there are no results. He stated that all other businesses had traceable accounts and hired lawyer Yan Yinwu to defend him. Judge Xu adjourned the hearing to a later date for further review.

Master Brother Attempts to Strangle Junior Brother 132

Claiming a Father's Murder

Qian Minglong, a tailor's apprentice at No. 1167 Zhonghua Road, Xiaoximen, is only a little over ten years old. His master brother, Zhang Hongfeng, who had already stopped working there, constantly suspected that Qian had slandered him, harboring a deep-seated grudge. The other day, Zhang came to the shop to hang around. Since it was late, he didn't leave and slept in the same bed with Qian. Unexpectedly, after Qian fell asleep, Zhang used a trouser belt to loop around Qian's neck. Both pulled on it, attempting to strangle Qian to death. Fortunately, Qian woke up and grabbed the belt with his hands, shouting for help. People in the shop heard the noise and all got up to investigate. They restrained Zhang. Qian's neck had already been scratched. Because the matter involved murder, the police were called to arrest Zhang and detain him in the Second District, Second Precinct. Yesterday, he was sent to the District Court. Prosecutor Yang interrogated him. Zhang confessed that Qian's father had plotted to kill his father, so he was avenging his father, which was the truth. However, Qian said that his father had no feud with Zhang's father. The official, based on Zhang's admission of murder, ordered him to be detained pending punishment.

Enjoying the Cool Air, Suddenly Encountering an Enemy 133

Jiang Zaitang Suffers Two Axe Wounds

His Life is in Grave Danger

Jiang Zaitang, a native of Ningbo, residing at No. 8 Run'an Lane, Ximen Road, in the French Concession, is twenty-five years old. Last night, he went to Pin Chengliang in Lane 5, nearby, to enjoy the cool air. Suddenly, five or six enemies came, pulled out sharp axes, and without asking any questions, struck Jiang's right leg with one axe, breaking his tibia. Another axe struck his right waist, penetrating about six inches deep, with blood gushing like a spring. He fainted on the spot. The assailants, seeing that their purpose had been achieved, all left swaggeringly. When Jiang's family heard the alarm and arrived, Zaitang was barely breathing and his life was hanging by a thread. They immediately hired a car and sent him to Renji Hospital for treatment. It is said that his life is in great danger.

Opposing the Feetham Report 136

Joint Declaration by Over Seventy Labor Unions

The Shanghai Publishing Industry Union, Postal Workers' Union, First District Water and Electricity Industry Union, First District Cotton Textile Industry Union, First District Shipbuilding Industry Union, First District Papermaking Industry Union, First District Knitting Industry Union, First District Garment Industry Union, First District Carpentry Industry Union, First District Cleaning Industry Union, Municipal Sauce Industry Union, Municipal Pharmaceutical Industry Union, Municipal Newspaper Distribution Industry Union, Municipal Pharmaceutical Trade Union, Municipal Western Cuisine Industry Union, Municipal Hat Making Industry Union, Municipal Customs Brokerage Industry Union, Municipal Tea and Pastry Industry Union, Municipal Match Industry Union, Municipal Starch Noodle Industry Union, Municipal Letterpress Printing Industry Union, Municipal Shipyard Woodworkers Union, Municipal Water and Electricity Company Union, and over seventy other labor unions issued a declaration opposing the Feetham Report. At this time when the National Government formally announced the recovery of the concessions, "the Shanghai Municipal Council and the continuously published so-called Feetham Report" praised the goodness of the concession system and repeatedly stated that, given the current situation, the recovery of the concessions was almost impossible. These kinds of fallacies are infuriating to read. The position of the concessions has no legal basis, and the governing power of the concessions was entirely seized. Recovering this seized governing power has long been a unanimous goal of the entire country. Now, fortunately, the National Government is fully negotiating and is gradually seeing progress. However, the Shanghai Municipal Council, at this time of its demise, did not hesitate to spend the heavy money paid by the citizens to hire a judge, Feetham, from South Asia who was accustomed to ruling colonies, to issue this

fallacy, using it as a defense. It only shows that their efforts are becoming increasingly futile. The Feetham Report clearly states in the opening remarks: "To advise the Municipal Council, to assist the Council in planning construction projects, and to provide reasonable and adequate protection for the commercial interests of foreigners engaged in business in Shanghai" (English version, Volume 1, page 5). Although it was later stated that the words "foreigners" were deleted, Sima Zhao's intentions are known to everyone. Our associations dare to formally tell all friendly foreign merchants that the development of international commerce is entirely based on equality and friendship of mutual understanding. If, on the one hand, you firmly hold onto the illegal rights that have been seized, and on the other hand, you want to develop the commercial interests of foreigners, this is truly like wanting to go south by driving the chariot north, which is simply impossible. If friendly foreign merchants do not want to harm the goodwill of the nationals of the country where they are located and seek the development of their commerce, they should urge their own government to immediately return the seized governing power of the concessions to China. Otherwise, being deceived by a few unscrupulous merchants and wanting to maintain this concession system, which is approaching its end, and struggling against the wishes of the people of our entire country, the dire consequences can be imagined. What to choose, we hope that the wise and intelligent friendly foreign merchants will decide. Our associations also want to say that the content of the Feetham Report is almost entirely filled with statements that violate the facts and disregard international etiquette. Since he brazenly dares to issue such fallacies, then our nationals should also demand that the government immediately expel him from the country. At the same time, we demand that the Shanghai Municipal Council immediately withdraw this Feetham Report that disregards international etiquette. If there are any unfilial nationals who dare to associate with this kind of arrogant foreigner, or even be used by them, our nationals will all regard them as national traitors and abandon them together. This is our solemn declaration.

Resolution of the Bus Pass Issue for the Gaochangmiao Arsenal Workers 139

Regarding the previous dispute between the China General Edison Company and the workers of the Arsenal and Jiangnan Shipyard over bus passes, it was resolved through mediation by both parties. General Manager Lu of the company sent Lu Zhonglin, the head of the Lighting Department, to negotiate with Director Guo of the Arsenal and Director Ma of the Shipyard, and a solution was reached. The original old bus passes will be exchanged for new ones, and the number of passes will be slightly increased by the Arsenal and Shipyard. The company's bus pass subsidy fee will be implemented starting from July 1st. The Arsenal originally had 2,300 bus passes with a monthly subsidy of 200 yuan, and the Longhua Arsenal Branch had 1,000 bus passes with a subsidy of 30 yuan. Now, the Arsenal has requested the company to increase the number of bus passes by 570, for a total of 3,870. The subsidy fee will be increased by 20% based on the previous price. The Jiangnan Shipyard originally had 1,500 bus passes with a monthly subsidy of 200 yuan, and now they are adding 780 passes, which will also be increased by 20%. The added bus passes will be priced accordingly. The new bus passes have been affixed with photos and divided into two or three grades. Yesterday, the company distributed them, and they were allowed to be exchanged for new passes starting yesterday. Director Guo of the Arsenal issued a notice stating: "Notice regarding the matter of bus rides for workers of this Arsenal. The workers of this Arsenal are now riding the China General Edison Company's trams. The company has changed to new passes, which have been distributed and claimed by the Arsenal's Labor Union. All old passes will be invalidated from July 1st. From now on, if anyone still carries an old pass to ride the bus, the company should check and have the person return it for cancellation. This notice is hereby issued for your information."

Resolution of the Strike at the British American Tobacco Factory 141

All the workers in the tin-packaging section of the old British American Tobacco factory in Pudong went on strike because they opposed the factory's failure to follow the original practice of automatically adding seven long-term workers. Their protests were ineffective, leading to a unanimous work stoppage for over ten days. After multiple negotiations, a satisfactory resolution could not be reached. It is now learned that yesterday at 1:00 PM, negotiations continued at the factory. Labor representatives Chen Peizhong and Gu Ruofeng, management representative Secretary Wei, and Chairman Xu Zhi of the Social Affairs Bureau discussed the matter for a long time and agreed on seven conditions for resolution. Both parties were satisfied, and the resolution was announced. It was decided that all workers would resume work today. The conditions for resolution are recorded below: (1) Future hiring methods will be handled according to the factory's original practices. (2) The seven temporary workers will be changed to short-term workers. After work resumes, the factory will immediately add seven long-term workers according to the old practice. (3) Male and female workers in the tin-packaging section will be paid wages for seven days during the strike. (4) Workers in other sections who entered the factory and registered during the strike will be paid wages. Contract workers in various sections should negotiate with Factory Director Helan Tuo. (5) Rice subsidies will be paid during the strike. (6) Sudi Huate and Lao Ba

Si will be given warnings by the factory. (7) Four old workers will voluntarily resign from the factory, and the factory will provide them with a one-time allowance.

Street Cleaning Handed Over to the Bureau of Public Health 142

Effective Yesterday

Joint Notice by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Public Health and the Public Security Bureau: Joint notice regarding the matter of street cleaning. The Municipal Government, in accordance with instruction No. 6575, decided at the 170th Municipal Conference to transfer street cleaning to this Public Security Bureau for a six-month trial period. This was announced on February 1st of this year when this Public Security Bureau took over the handling of the matter. Recently, it has been found that the trial period is about to expire, and the central government has promulgated the responsibilities of various municipal bureaus, stating that street cleaning should be under the jurisdiction of the Bureau of Public Health. This Public Security Bureau submitted a report to the Municipal Government on June 6th, proposing to return it to the Bureau of Public Health. The 183rd Municipal Conference decided that starting from July 1st, the street cleaning affairs will be handed over to this Bureau of Public Health. In addition to reporting and handing over the matter for continued handling, this notice is hereby issued for public knowledge. June 25th, 20th year of the Republic of China. Hu Hongji, Director of the Bureau of Public Health, and Chen Xizeng, Director of the Public Security Bureau.

Sheng Sheng's Soda Water is Selling Well 146

Its fresh aroma, clean water, and pure carbonation have won the praise of people both domestic and abroad. In order to facilitate various sectors of society, the factory has established a wholesale outlet in Jili Lane, Diandang Street, in the French Concession, which is managed by Messrs. Sun and Chen from Shanghai.
