Free Talk

World Tidbits 152

— Sea Guest

The Train That Obeys Commands

A train is a mechanical, soulless thing. How can it understand people's commands? However, this actually happened. In London, England, a newly invented electric train model was displayed. Experts tested it, and it was found that by simply shouting "Stop," the engine would immediately stop. By shouting "Go," the engine would start and move forward. It is said that the inner workings rely on a transmitter and the fluctuation of sound waves to determine movement and stopping. Its structure is very complex.

The Nine-Foot, Nine-Inch Long Fish

A very large tuna was recently caught in the ocean fourteen miles off the coast of Scarborough in northern England. It measured nine feet and nine inches long and weighed six hundred pounds. In the fish world, it can be considered a giant. According to experienced fishermen, such a fish may be caught in the North Sea because the water in the North Sea was warmer three years ago, and tuna had appeared.

A 10,000-Year Lease

No matter which country in the world, the term for leasing real estate is at most a few decades. Unexpectedly, the town of Lahti in Finland leased a piece of land to an oil company as a fueling station and unexpectedly signed a 10,000-year lease. This can be considered a new record in leases.

Glimpses of the Capital 153

— Cheng Zhizheng

It has been two years since I left the capital. Recently, after finishing my studies, I traveled with a friend for sightseeing again. What I saw and heard was quite noteworthy. Therefore, I will describe it.

The area beside Zhongshan Road was once extremely desolate, but now it has become a prosperous marketplace and political center. Great and magnificent buildings are everywhere. The Saga Bay area is where various ministries are concentrated. Those that have been completed include the Ministry of Railways, the Ministry of the Navy, and the Ministry of Military Affairs. Those under construction include the Ministry of Communications and the Ministry of Finance. The scale is astonishing. The official residence of the Ministry of Railways is palace-style and extremely beautiful. The Ministry of Communications, which is under construction, is opposite the Ministry of Railways in a similar style, but its grandeur seems to surpass it.

The Bund in Shanghai is a bank street, and Simalu is a bookstore street. The bank street in Nanjing is in the Daxing Palace area. Various banks have marked the construction foundations, but construction has not yet started. The bookstore street is in Huapai Lou, with more than a dozen bookstores. The newly built roads in Nanjing are wider than those in Shanghai and sometimes have narrower stone roads built next to the asphalt roads, specifically for horse carriages. The atmosphere is majestic, and the power of construction is great.

Public buses used to be operated by several companies, but now they are monopolized by Xinghua. Because there were many disputes with female ticket sellers, they are no longer used. It is said that Xinghua Company is run by a certain important person. Therefore, all soldiers must buy tickets. It is said that buying tickets is quite funny. Regardless of the distance, soldiers only pay three copper coins, probably to save face.

Sound movies are very popular in Beijing. The National Theater is particularly outstanding. It mostly shows famous films from Shanghai, and the seats are full. However, in terms of construction, it is still far behind Shanghai. The sound is also unclear. The singing of female singers in the Confucius Temple area has been sluggish recently, probably due to the trends of the times and natural elimination.

Aircraft training takes place every day, and its various performances are particularly astonishing. Sometimes they tumble left and right, and sometimes they speed up and down. It is heart-stirring and cannot be watched to the end. Incidents that lead to accidents are also heard every day. Lately, military tensions have increased, and aircraft have become more important. German and American instructors are working hard to train them. It is said that a large team will be dispatched soon.

Old Youngsters in the Art World 154

— Zheng Yimei

"Old Youngster" is a different name for amaranth, a wonderful embellishment for autumn fences. However, what I call "Old Youngsters" refers to Zhao Banbo, Wu Ziding, two old men, and Ma Wanli, a young man. The changes of nature, the divine hand, and the lonely art world are all brightened and colored. This is a good story. I once saw the exhibition of Old Youngsters. It still lingers in my mind. Wanli is a master of flowers. His works are all outstanding and refreshing, with a clear fragrance. Mr. Zeng Nongran calls him "creating spring everywhere," which is not empty praise. A daffodil with only a few strokes is full of elegance. Xuanxuan's charm is relaxed and natural. He can be regarded as a masterpiece. Banbo's works are characterized by sparseness and distance. He resembles Qing Teng and Xue Ge. This is why Banbo took the characters Teng and Xue as the name of his apartment building. Ziding Wu Ruifen is the most skilled in figures and ladies. He has deeply understood the essence of Gai Qixiang. "Girls Returning to Wash Clothes in the Bamboo Noise" shows his skill in painting bamboo. Su Changgong said, "When painting bamboo, one must first have a bamboo in one's mind." Ziding must have bamboo in his heart. "Begging for Skills" and "Seeking Plum Blossoms" are also meticulously crafted. It is not easy to find them in Shanghai. Last winter, Ziding went to Shexian, Anhui, to serve as the county secretary. With his nature of a free-spirited person, he could not bear the trouble of official documents and politics. He came to Shanghai a few days ago, bringing with him several pines from Huangshan. The cost of transportation was several hundred strings, but he did not hesitate. Ziding is good at chanting and has many poems commemorating his travels. He traveled along the Fuchun River by boat and passed Yanling Lai, which happened to be in a dream at night. Therefore, he wrote the line "Stealing past the Fishing Terrace in the deep night." Ziding lives in Wu Zhong Luqiu Fangxiang. He indulges in poetry and wine and enjoys painting. With his youthful face and rosy complexion, he is truly a celestial being.

Small Recipes 155

— Yang Yixiao

Vegetable Soup: Take dried bamboo shoots, soak them until soft, and tear them into small pieces. Take one slice each of center-cut duck meat, ham, and *qiao* bamboo shoots. Shape them like a bundle of firewood. Stew them in chicken soup until tender. This is called vegetable soup.

Crab Eggs: Cut off the claws and legs of fresh crabs. Pour egg whites on top and stir-fry two or three times, then stop.

Steamed Carp: Use the head of a carp. Add chicken soup and slices of ham. Place it on top of the rice pot to steam. The flavor is particularly delicious.

Frozen Pigeon: Chop the pigeon into small pieces. Braise it in dark soy sauce and medicinal oil. After it is removed from the pot, place it in the refrigerator so that it solidifies into a jelly. Sprinkle a little licorice and fennel powder on the outside.

Shrimp Brain: When peeling shrimp, take the brains. Briefly soak them in boiling water. Mix them with soy sauce, sesame oil, and agar-agar. The flavor is incredibly fresh and tender.

A Study of Kissing and Eyebrow Painting 156

— Sun Linchang

"Kissing" is a passionate expression of love. A couple in love touches lips, sweetly intoxicated. But fashionable people today desperately imitate Western customs, thinking that "kissing" also comes from the West. Little do they know that this kind of romantic affair already existed in China long ago. However, Western customs are public, while Chinese ones are secret. Like the ancient poems about courtesans, "A little bit of red lips tasted by ten thousand guests" is what we now call "kissing." Also, Guo Sheren's "Fei concubine's lips are as sweet as candy," and the Romance of the West Chamber's "mouth seeking tongue" depict "kissing" with what resemblance. "Kissing" is a heady thing. "A lover's kiss is worth more than ten *yi* of gold." However, according to a certain hygienist, "Kissing is a medium for infectious diseases. Each kiss results in the exchange of millions of microorganisms between lips." Affectionate compatriots of both sexes should pay attention.

The poem about painting eyebrows says, "This child is clear and bright." "Clear" refers to the eyes, and "bright" refers to the eyebrows. Also, "moth eyebrows" are said to be the most beautiful eyebrows of a beautiful woman. In ancient times, eyebrows were naturally beautiful, so grooming was done, not painting. Song Yu's "Summoning the Soul" says, "Moth eyebrows, beautiful eyes, and beautiful instructions." This refers to painting. Later, Wen Jun went far away with Jiang Xian's beauty, Jing Zhao's charming eyebrows, and Ying Jie's eyebrow habits, all of which were painters. Emperor Ming of Tang had a "Ten Eyebrow Diagram," such as horizontal clouds and crescent moons. Eyebrow painting in the Five Dynasties palace was classified into ten types: (1) Kaiyuan's imperial love, (2) Little Mountain, (3) Five Peaks, (4) Three Peaks, (5) Drooping Pearl, (6) Moon Ridge, (7) Powder Tip, (8) Containing Smoke, (9) Brushing Clouds, (10) Inverted Halo. It is unknown why no one pays attention to it in modern times.

A Friend's Child 157

— Tang Chengxin

A friend of mine has a child who is five years old. He is as thin and weak as an old man. He has been taking tonics all year round, but they are not effective. Recently, he suffered from typhoid fever, followed by aphonia. The doctor looked worried. His mother loves him very much and weeps all day long, not knowing what to do. Considering that his family is wealthy, if he had been properly cared for, he should have been stronger than ordinary children. However, love was not given in the right way, and the principles of child physiology were neglected. As a result, his illness became increasingly obvious. Only then did they seek miraculous medicine, but it was too late. Now, I will briefly describe one or two of the inappropriate aspects of his upbringing and care to inform those who raise children, so that they know what to pay attention to and do not repeat his mistakes. My friend, if he hears of this, will hopefully not take offense.

When the child was first born, a wet nurse fed him milk. Sometimes, he would occasionally spit up his milk, which was mistakenly taken as overeating. He was forbidden to be fed again. The child cried from hunger, but no one cared. Until he was four years old, he was still not weaned. He was not fed rice either. All year round, he was confined to a high pavilion, and his windows were tightly closed. Whenever the weather was slightly cold, he was dressed in double the amount of clothing. He became as bloated as a roly-poly toy. As a result, the child's body became weaker and weaker. The parents still did not know to change their ways, as if they were afraid that he would not get sick. Although their love for their child was deep, their intentions were not blameworthy. However, because of improper upbringing and care, they ultimately harmed his body, which is truly regrettable. Wags say that their neglect of science is no different from intentionally using science to put a child in danger. I wonder what excuses these parents will use to justify themselves?

Travel Notes in India (59) 158

— Linghua

The university buildings are neat and magnificent. I told Mr. Wenke Tolun that Indians do not pay attention to politics but focus on religion and philosophy. If Gandhi's doctrines spread to villages everywhere in the future, your India will once again practice anarchism. Today, the people have never paid attention to politics. There is no need to explain politics. Just attach them to school districts. Set up more work-study villages. It will be enough for leaders like Gandhi to govern. I think if India truly has a day of freedom, this will also be a dream.

Indian students are very polite and follow the rules in an orderly manner. They have no arrogance. They are not like Chinese students who agitate for trends. There is still no trend of students being the masters and teachers being the guests. They still maintain good habits. I visited their dining hall. It is not like our country where they eat at tables and chairs. Instead, they sit on the ground, which is either covered with wooden boards or carpets. Each person uses a copper plate. The plate contains two dishes and rice. They eat with their hands. Generally, they eat rice at noon and wheat cakes in the evening. The cakes are not much different from those in China. Only the northern-made single cakes are smaller in India and sometimes have oil added.

On the 25th, students guided me through the garden. It is said that this city has many gardens, some public and some private. I went to the garden and saw many flowers. The flower beds are in various shapes and are very beautiful. Indians love flowers and pick them to offer to Buddha. The ancient tradition of burning incense and scattering flowers still exists today. The flowers do not wither in all seasons, which is a characteristic of India. But I feel that not many tropical flowers are fragrant. On this day, I discussed with the professors and asked me to make a declaration for the Asian Education Association, briefly stating the prosperity of Asian culture since ancient times. All races and religions originate from Asia. No saints teach killing. Since the beginning of modern education, we should use humanism to fairly govern society and strive for the great unity of the world. This responsibility requires the awakening and connection of Asian people. Moreover, after the war, Europeans longed for the westward spread of Eastern culture. Therefore, we should strive to organize and promote world peace. As for pan-Asian connection, it is of course a big problem. However, as far as I know and from past experience, the longing for connection is greatest among Indians. In China, it is hardly felt. This is because Chinese people do not pay attention to this, and very few people do. Or it may be because their vision is short-sighted. As for those who can connect with each other, Indians can connect with Buddhist countries such as China and Japan. Of course, there is no problem. However, it is very difficult to connect with Muslim countries. If Chinese people do it, it is relatively easier. Muslims have very good feelings towards Chinese people, which is false for Indians. It is not difficult to send people to Turkey to connect.

Rotary Club Storytelling

？？？（九） 159

— Xu Zhuodai

After Yue Ru went downstairs, Zi Liang closed the door of the attic. As he sat down again, he couldn't help but think of the past. Before he was married, he often thought, "In the future, when I have a wife, I will go home every night. I will read under the lamp, and my wife will sit next to me and keep me company. She will do some needlework and keep me company until the night is quiet. Wouldn't that be interesting?" Who knew that after marriage, the ideal and reality were so far apart. Now, if Zi Liang wants to study hard, he absolutely cannot let her stay by his side. Otherwise, she will only make noise, how can he do anything? Zi Liang also thought, "If my finances were more relaxed, I would definitely find a temple to rent a room in, so that I could study hard and avoid this beautiful demon from constantly缠不淸楚. If this continues, I might as well live at school starting in the second half of the year."

The door of the attic creaked open, and Yue Ru stood smiling at the door, holding a large bowl in her hand:

"Stop studying! Snacks are here!"

She brought it to Zi Liang's table. When Zi Liang looked, there were seven or eight different things in this large bowl: a sesame cake, a steamed bun, a glutinous rice ball, a piece of square cake, a fried dough stick, a scallion pancake, a small bread, like a ten-scene fruit platter put together; but each item was only one piece.

"What is this? It's not some kind of sample, everything is just one piece."

"Difficult questions, only you can ask! When I ask you what snack you want, you say anything. How can I guess what's in your stomach? I can only buy a few more items, and there will always be something you like!"

Zi Liang didn't listen to her reasoning. He was hungry enough, so he had to take it and eat. But it was already late, so he didn't dare to eat too much, leaving a small half in the bowl:

"Take it away!"

"After filling your stomach, you want to drive away the person who provided the food. You have no conscience!"

The madam took the big bowl away; but she didn't go downstairs, she went to the front room. After a while, only the sound of constant footsteps could be heard from the floorboards. She was 拉拉拉拉 singing, apparently practicing dancing there. Once, a friend came to visit Pan Zi Liang and sat downstairs. At that time, it just so happened that the madam was also practicing dancing upstairs. The friend heard the sound on the floorboards and looked up. Unexpectedly, the dust from the floorboards fell down and landed right in the friend's eyes, making it impossible to open them and impossible to remove them. Later, they called a barber to help remove it.

After the tenth line of yesterday's article, the phrase "is really a new record exceeding Pan's ancestral generations" was omitted.

The Mid-term Interest Rates in Financial Closure are Quiet 160

Yesterday, all the major Chinese and foreign banks were closed for the half-year accounting, so the market situation showed a very calm attitude. Even the gatherings of the money market were particularly brief, gathering and dispersing quickly. The time was less than half of the usual time, resulting in not much competition in interest rate prices. The interest rate for both the morning and afternoon markets was the same, at 7 *qian*, 2 *fen*, 6 *li*, and 2.5 *hao*. This was mostly similar to the price at the end of last month. The silver interest rate was 8 *fen* in the morning market and 7 *fen* in the afternoon market, which was also very average. The amount of remittance bills made was 455,000 in the morning market and only 300,500 in the afternoon market. There were no transactions in the banknote market in either the morning or afternoon. However, the out-of-market banknotes were 135,000 *jiao* in the morning market and 40,000 *jiao* in the afternoon market. The money shops received and delivered 5,780,000 in foreign public bills and more than 48,000,000 in silver public bills. The transactions of small money shops were more than 300,000. The remittances from various places were more than 500,000. The market situation for auxiliary coins was as follows: Jiangnan small dollars were 6 *qian*, 4 *fen*, and 8.5 *li* in the morning market, and the same price in the afternoon market. A Glimpse of the Huge Volume of Inflow and Outflow at the End of the Half-Year 161

The day before yesterday was the end of June, which is the big period for the half-year accounting.

The receiving and delivering procedures for the silver and money industry were more complicated than usual. Therefore, most banks sorted things out all night the night before. Many were still not finished by 6 or 7 o'clock yesterday morning, which shows one aspect of the complexity of the procedures. According to the current survey, the amount of receipts and deliveries for bills and various routine remittances, taxes, etc. reached more than 100 million. The amount of special remittances and settlements was also tens of millions. The amount of silver public bills received and delivered by the money shops was as high as 81,941,500 *liang*, which is a new record. According to previous years, a small number of merchants still adhered to the abandoned calendar for the half-year end, so the receiving, delivering and sorting times were different. This year, the dates have been unified, so the procedures on that day were particularly busy.

Yesterday was the first day of the half-year accounting holiday for various foreign firms in this port. All banks were closed, and there were no foreign exchange transactions. The foreign firm silk transactions will be suspended for both yesterday and today.

The Amount of Spring Dried Cocoons Transported to Shanghai from the Suzhou Area Has Been Greatly Reduced 169

Only Two-Tenths of Previous Years: The Amount of Cocoons Transported to Shanghai is About 70,000 *dan*

This year's spring silkworms in the Suzhou area have suffered greatly from the weather. The cocoon production is unusually poor, totaling only three-tenths of the normal year. Moreover, there are few high-quality cocoons and many inferior ones. Although a small number of silk cocoon merchants went to various regions to set up shops to collect cocoons, the cocoon prices were unusually high, and inferior goods were rejected. Therefore, the amount collected was very small. The amount of dried cocoons transported to Shanghai has been greatly reduced, and transportation is about to come to an end. Except for the farmers who spin their own土丝, and the silk merchants in Zhenjiang, Wuxi, and Suzhou who retain raw materials for their own use, the amount of cocoons transported to Shanghai from various regions totals about 70,000 *dan*.

The Shipment of Wuyuan Zicha Tea is Still Strong 170

Mountain households in Wuyuan County have been picking Zicha tea for ten days. The needs of various firms are also strong. The price has been raised to 7 *jiao* per *jin*. Since the Shanghai telegram reported a drop in the price of Zhenmei tea by 50 or 60 *liang*, the firms have been accepting it, uniformly lowering the price to 5 *jiao* per *jin*. The firms that lack tea have a large demand for the abundant shipment of Zicha tea. There are occasional secret bids of 6 *jiao* to search for goods. In recent days, mountain households have been picking tea continuously. General tea merchants are also searching for goods overnight. The shipment is very strong. Judging from the concentration of Zicha tea growth on the tea trees, there is still a large amount available for picking and production.

Luzhuang Zhenmei European Sales Slightly Active 171

Yesterday, Baochang, Yongxing, Duder, and other firms in Luzhuang, Zhenmei, and green tea from Wuyuan, Tunxi, and other places all had purchases. Other merchants also sent many telegrams, and the market was slightly more active than before. Among them,抽芯 goods were particularly popular, but sales bids tended to be weak. There were sporadic transactions of Zhenmei, Xiumei, Gongxi, and other green teas. Gongxi saw a drop of 14 or 15 *liang*. Zhenmei and Xiumei also fell by 5 or 6 *liang*. The green tea market is still difficult to be optimistic about. Both Chinese and foreign tea merchants hope that the British and American exchange rates will stabilize quickly to determine the final direction.

Sugar Market Quiet and Flat 172

This Factory's Crystal Sugar Opens at a Decrease of 3 *qian*

Yesterday's sugar market telegrams: The price of Cuban spot sugar was 1.375. The price of New York sugar futures for September was 1.31, and for December was 1.40, each down 2 *fen* from the previous telegram. The price for March next year was 1.48, and for May was 1.54, also each down 1 *fen*. The prices of current and forward sugar in Java were both 8.125, with no increase or decrease from the previous price. The guild market's planning was quiet, and there were few transactions. Dutch sugar No. 24 coarse grain white sugar was still bid at 11 *liang* and 2 *qian*, and high-quality coarse grain was 11 *liang* and 3 *qian*. No. 20 medium grain white sugar was 10 *liang* and 6 *qian*. Transactions were scarce. The market shape was sluggish. The import and export of Japanese sugar was also lazy. "N" mark was 10 *liang* and 8.5 *qian*, TK mark was the same price, YT mark was 10 *liang* and 8 *qian*, YRO mark was 10 *liang* and 5.75 *qian*, YP mark was 11 *liang* and 1.5 *qian*, TX mark was 11 *liang* and 1 *qian*, and TM mark was 10 *liang* and 6.75 *qian*.

"SH" mark was 10 *liang* and 6.25 *qian*, "J" mark was 11 *liang* and 2 *qian*, with no ups and downs compared to the previous price, and the market shape was flat. The number of transactions was still quiet. Shanghai factory's crystal ice opened with several hundred bags. The Ren character price was 14 *liang*, and the Qian character price was 13 *liang* and 9 *qian*, a steep drop of 3 *qian* from the previous price, and the market was weak.

North-South Goods: Yesterday, the New Guangdong Lychee Opened at 38 *liang* 173

Yesterday, the Guangbang firms in the North Market transported ten boxes of new dried lychees again. Samples were immediately shown. The color was still good, but the body was very soft. This was because they were transported to Shanghai early to catch the new season. Then, it was acquired by a certain firm in the South Market at 38 *liang*, and the trend was stable.

Piece Goods, Hats, and Flannel are Selling Lively 174

In recent days, the weather has been hot, and the transaction of wool goods and flannels has predictably decreased. Most of what was opened in the guild were writing goods. Yesterday, only small hats and flannels were selling quite lively. The hat workshops in Chenghuang Temple and Jiumudi on this street, and Sanguantang in Hongkou, all had needs. Goods ranging from 1 *liang* and several *qian* to 4 *liang* of silver were all being opened. The spot goods and those with an extension of the due date were split evenly. It is heard that domestic Zhang

Hua goods were also being sold, with each yard being calculated at 1 *yuan*, 3 *liang*, and 5 *qian* net.

Hardware: More Than 1,000 Boxes of British Tinplate Open 175

Yesterday's hardware transactions were very bleak due to the bank's accounting relationship. However, the business of British tinplate had the momentum of spring grass after rain yesterday. It is estimated that more than 1,400 boxes were opened. It was found that 850 boxes were 90 pounds each, and the rest were all 100 pounds. The price of 90 pounds was 15 *liang* and 5 *qian*, and the price of 100 pounds was 16 *liang* and 2.5 *qian*. It is heard that the purchasers were all from the Tianjin gang, and the decoration of the factories on this street was also quite strong.

Art Circle

On Figure Painting 187

— By Kinoshita Takanori, translated by Chen Bao Yi

...This is to have me explain the techniques of figure painting, in an easy-to-understand manner, to the extent that even amateurs (non-specialists) can understand.

However, it is said that normally when starting to learn painting, one starts with still life, then landscapes, and then figures, in that order. Figure painting is comparatively the most difficult, because during sketching, figures cannot be kept still like still life. Moreover, even a slight error can be noticed and felt to be inappropriate, so it is not easy to achieve satisfactory results... Therefore, being able to paint figure paintings normally is considered like graduating. However, if we try to paint various kinds of paintings, even seemingly easy still life paintings or figure paintings, we eventually feel unsure which one is ultimately more difficult.

Therefore, regardless of landscape, regardless of still life, the main thing is that we can create good paintings, and that will do.

As for saying...how should still life paintings be painted to become good paintings, how should landscape paintings be painted, and how should figure paintings be painted to be good... These kinds of questions... However, I feel that there is no fixed and unchanging rule in painting that dictates how a certain kind of painting must be painted with a certain technique. Moreover, what kind of painting is considered a "good painting"? This question is not as easy to resolve as it sounds... This, I don't know how to explain, and other than saying that it is difficult to explain, there is no way.

Now, what I want to say to painting students is... if you want to paint, then first pick up the palette and brush, stand in front of the canvas, express what you want to depict, that which stirs your artistic feelings, and paint it on the canvas. By pursuing what you want to express, "technique" will naturally emerge. The deeper the pursuit, the better the painting will ultimately be.

But, now if you ask me... "You often paint figure paintings, so what order do you follow when painting?"... Since that's the case, I might as well reveal my own immature experience. I would be fortunate if it could benefit the readers.

...Let's talk about my experience.

When I paint, I rarely think about theory.

Now, suppose I am painting a half-body portrait of a woman. Let's talk about the order of painting... At first, from the expression on the face, the color of the skin, and the feeling of the body, I look for a figure that I want to paint. Then, I ask her to settle into a pose, and then I pay attention to the background and the colors of the clothes, the color of the face, the overall harmony, the shape of the pose, etc., and make adjustments.

Then, based on this, I select the size and shape (e.g., square or rectangular) of the canvas and determine the layout of the figure on the canvas. Once that's settled, I first start painting with "harmony" and "tone" that come from the contrast of colors.

At the beginning, I often start by painting the hair, the color of the hairline and forehead, and the color of the background, to create the basic tone of the entire picture... I often do it this way, proceeding with a feeling of understanding "nature," and always keeping "the reality of the object" in mind. I pursue the mass of the object according to the harmony of colors. However, if I continue to paint like this for three days, the tone becomes chaotic in the middle, and I eventually fail... This is my experience.

I was once asked... "What colors do you use for the color of your background?" Although I painted this color there, I remember answering him like this... "I'm not sure, it seems like Moir do Pecho, Ochre, Jauoe, B1, and Ceruleum are mixed in." I thought that rather than forgetting what colors I mixed, it was that I hadn't paid attention to this point in the first place.

Just like this, I am unconscious when I paint. Therefore, it is difficult for me to explain the order of painting. The explanation above seems to be of no help.

Although the above is titled a talk on figure painting, I have said that there is no fixed and unchanging technique in terms of technique. However, since ancient times, not limited to figure painting, many painters have been troubled by painting and have made various considerations, and have seen famous paintings, and have separated their theories to explain the method of painting... Naturally, we also know that even if we paint according to theory, we may not create a good painting. However, I believe that if we use theory as a reference, we can benefit a lot. Here, it would be best to describe this so-called "technique." However, "technique" is not a simple thing, so I will have to leave it for another opportunity to describe it again.

Literary Anecdotes

Masculine Literature 188

— Jun Xiao

When the Greek poet Fheuos Rigas looked down from the peak of Mount Asos, he shouted with tears in his eyes,

"It is not the time to cry, it is the time to do!"

"Cry" is a feminine action, "do" is a masculine action, "cry" literature is feminine literature, "do" literature is masculine literature.

The style of the work shows a kind of passionate stimulation, which invisibly inspires and moves people greatly, as solemn and great as the sun god climbing out of Mount Olympus, and at the same time, it is a yearning for the pursuit of strength. This is a symbol of "masculine" literature.

Now, we know that the nation originating from the Pamir Plateau is approaching a stage of danger and turmoil. It is extremely clear that it is absolutely not easy to achieve the hope of freedom and equality by not "doing" but only dreaming of peaceful means and passive resistance. Therefore, in this situation, all that belongs to courageously moving forward, is rich in stimulation, | masculine literature, is an extreme need at the moment. However, in the past, it has given us disappointment. Except for those articles that throw life into a glass of wine, entrust life to the velvet-like breast of a woman, and gently wither with self-pity, what we hope for has never been seen.

Recently, after reading the two novels in the fifth issue of "Avant-Garde Monthly," that is exactly what I felt in my heart. One is "On the Longhai Line" by Huang Zhenxia, and the other is "A Momentary Revolution" by Wan Guo'an. Both of these are literary works depicting war, just as Dr. Li said, "It is not the time to cry, it is the time to do!" Works with this nature appear in China, a country of moderation and peace. This phenomenon has given us a bit of joy in loneliness, because what we need now is precisely this kind.

Su Manshu and Others in the Surabaya Era 189

Su Manshu's poems have been widely recited for a long time, and Su Manshu's life has attracted even more attention. Recently, Mr. Tang Yunyu, while traveling in Surabaya, compiled a book entitled "Su Manshu and Others in the Surabaya Era." The table of contents is as follows:

Upper Section: Regarding various aspects of Su Manshu's time in Surabaya. (1) Preface, (2) A Brief Biography of Su Xuanying, (3) The Process of Being Hired by the Surabaya Chinese Association, (4) Manshu's Foster Mother, (5) Friends and Students at the Time, (6) Surviving Scattered Writings, (7) Letters from Nibang, Qiji, and Shou to Manshu, (8) Four Anecdotes: A, Lost Coin; B, A Glimpse of Generosity; C, Prince Fu's Habitual Youthful Indulgence, Loving Beauty More Than the Country; D, One Drunken Evening.

Lower Section: Feelings After Reading "The Complete Works of Su Manshu." (1) Written After "Textual Research on the New Biography of Su Xuanying," A, Regarding "Xuan Ying's Father Died a Few Months After His Birth," B, The Implication of the Chronology, C, Whether or Not the Person Xue Mei Existed, D, Unpublished Works That Could Not Be Passed Down to the World, E, South American Yekodar Country and Yapo Slope, F, A Second Discussion of Xue Mei, (2) Random Talk by a Monk, (3) Appendix.

This book began in September of the nineteenth year. The author currently resides at the Surabaya Chinese School in Java.

Guidelines for Art World Contributions 190

(1) Articles are limited to news, reviews, and introductions related to recent art (painting, music, sculpture, architecture, drama, etc.) and literature, both domestic and foreign.

(2) Photographs are limited to recent portraits and works of domestic and foreign artists, and related images.

(3) Various photographs related to the text are permitted.

(4) Each article should not exceed 2,000 characters in length. Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(5) Each article should not exceed 2,000 characters in length.
